<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Comic strip created by Jim Davis</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the comic strip. For the title character, see <a href="/wiki/Garfield_(character)" title="Garfield (character)">Garfield (character)</a>. For the president, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Garfield" title="James Garfield">James Garfield</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Garfield_(disambiguation)" title="Garfield (disambiguation)">Garfield (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox infobox vevent"><tbody><tr><th class="infobox-above summary" colspan="2" style="font-style: italic; background-color: ; color:">Garfield</th></tr><tr><td class="infobox-image" colspan="2"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Garfieldand_friends.png"><img alt="Garfieldand friends.png" data-file-height="298" data-file-width="257" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/46/Garfieldand_friends.png/220px-Garfieldand_friends.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/46/Garfieldand_friends.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a><div class="infobox-caption">Center: <a href="/wiki/Garfield_(character)" title="Garfield (character)">Garfield</a>. <p><i><b>Garfield</b></i> is an American <a href="/wiki/Comic_strip" title="Comic strip">comic strip</a> created by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Davis_(cartoonist)" title="Jim Davis (cartoonist)">Jim Davis</a>. Originally published locally as <i>Jon</i> in 1976, then in nationwide <a href="/wiki/Print_syndication" title="Print syndication">syndication</a> from 1978 as <i>Garfield</i>, it chronicles the life of the title character <a href="/wiki/Garfield_(character)" title="Garfield (character)">Garfield</a> the cat, his human owner <a href="/wiki/Jon_Arbuckle" title="Jon Arbuckle">Jon Arbuckle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Odie" title="Odie">Odie</a> the dog. As of 2013, it was syndicated in roughly 2,580 newspapers and <a href="/wiki/Magazine" title="Magazine">journals</a> and held the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Record" title="Guinness World Record">Guinness World Record</a> for being the world's most widely <a href="/wiki/Print_syndication" title="Print syndication">syndicated</a> comic strip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BW1_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-BW1-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Though its setting is rarely mentioned in print, <i>Garfield</i> takes place in Jim Davis's hometown of <a href="/wiki/Muncie,_Indiana" title="Muncie, Indiana">Muncie, Indiana</a>, according to the television special <i><a href="/wiki/Happy_Birthday,_Garfield" title="Happy Birthday, Garfield">Happy Birthday, Garfield</a></i>. Common themes in the strip include Garfield's laziness, obsessive eating, love of <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lasagne" title="Lasagne">lasagna</a>, disdain of <a href="/wiki/Monday" title="Monday">Mondays</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Diet_(nutrition)" title="Diet (nutrition)">diets</a>. Garfield is also shown to manipulate people to get whatever he wants. The strip's focus is mostly on the interactions among Garfield, Jon, and Odie, but other recurring characters appear as well.
</p><p>On August 6, 2019, before its merger with <a href="/wiki/CBS_Corporation" title="CBS Corporation">CBS Corporation</a> to become ViacomCBS (now <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Global" title="Paramount Global">Paramount Global</a>), New York City–based <a href="/wiki/Viacom_(2005%E2%80%932019)" title="Viacom (2005–2019)">Viacom</a> announced that it would acquire <a href="/wiki/Paws,_Inc." title="Paws, Inc.">Paws, Inc.</a>, including most rights to the <i>Garfield</i> franchise (the comics, merchandise and animated cartoons). The deal did not include the rights to the live-action <i>Garfield</i> films,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> which are still owned by <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a> through its <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Studios" title="20th Century Studios">20th Century Studios</a> label, as well as the upcoming animated <i>Garfield</i> film which is set for worldwide distribution by <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures" title="Sony Pictures">Sony Pictures</a>, except in China, scheduled for 2024.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Jim Davis continues to make comics, and a new Garfield animated series is in production for Paramount Global subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steinberg_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steinberg-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc"/>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jim_Davis_cropped.jpg"><img class="thumbimage" data-file-height="339" data-file-width="209" decoding="async" height="324" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Jim_Davis_cropped.jpg/200px-Jim_Davis_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0c/Jim_Davis_cropped.jpg 1.5x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jim_Davis_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cartoonist <a href="/wiki/Jim_Davis_(cartoonist)" title="Jim Davis (cartoonist)">Jim Davis</a> is the creator of <i>Garfield</i>.</div></div></div>
<p>Cartoonist <a href="/wiki/Jim_Davis_(cartoonist)" title="Jim Davis (cartoonist)">Jim Davis</a> was born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Muncie,_Indiana" title="Muncie, Indiana">Muncie, Indiana</a>. In 1973, while working as an assistant for T.K. Ryan's <i><a href="/wiki/Tumbleweeds_(comic_strip)" title="Tumbleweeds (comic strip)">Tumbleweeds</a></i>, he created the comic strip <i><a href="/wiki/Gnorm_Gnat" title="Gnorm Gnat">Gnorm Gnat</a></i>, which ran only in the <i>Pendleton Times</i> of <a href="/wiki/Pendleton,_Indiana" title="Pendleton, Indiana">Pendleton, Indiana</a>, from 1973 to 1975 and met with little success. Davis had tried to <a href="/wiki/Print_syndication" title="Print syndication">syndicate</a> the strip, but was unsuccessful; he noted that one editor told him that his "art was good, his gags were great, [but] nobody can identify with bugs."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Twenty_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Twenty-5">[5]</a></sup> Davis decided to peruse current comic strips to determine what species of animal characters might be more popular. He felt that dogs were doing well, but noticed no prominent cats. Davis figured he could create a cat star, having grown up on a farm with twenty-five cats. Thus was created the character of Garfield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Twenty_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Twenty-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>Garfield, the star, was based on the cats Davis grew up around; he took his name and personality from Davis' grandfather, James A. Garfield Davis, whom he described as "a large, cantankerous man."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-6">[6]</a></sup> The name Jon Arbuckle came from a 1950s coffee commercial. Jon's roommate Lyman, added to give Jon someone to talk with, carried on the name of an earlier <i>Gnorm Gnat</i> character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Twenty_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-Twenty-5">[5]</a></sup> The final character was Lyman's dog Spot, who was renamed <a href="/wiki/Odie" title="Odie">Odie</a> so as to avoid confusion with a dog also named Spot in the comic strip <i><a href="/wiki/Boner%27s_Ark" title="Boner's Ark">Boner's Ark</a></i>. From 1976 to early 1978, these characters appeared in a strip called <i>Jon</i> which also ran in the <i>Times</i>. The <i>Jon</i> comic strip was largely unknown until 2019, when YouTuber <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quinton_Reviews" title="Quinton Reviews">Quinton Hoover</a> found several digital scans of the <i>Jon</i> publications from the Pendleton Community Library and Indiana State Library.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> <i>Jon</i> first appeared in the <i>Pendleton Times</i> on January 8, 1976, just two weeks after <i>Gnorm Gnat</i> ended.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/United_Media" title="United Media">United Feature Syndicate</a> accepted the strip for national distribution, which had been retitled <i>Garfield</i> on September 1, 1977, in March 1978 (ending its run in the <i>Times</i> on the 2nd) and made its nationwide debut in 41 newspapers on June 19 of that year (however, after a test run, the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> dropped it, only to reinstate it after readers' complaints).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BW1_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-BW1-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catty_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Catty-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Garfield-comparison.png"><img class="thumbimage" data-file-height="177" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0c/Garfield-comparison.png/300px-Garfield-comparison.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/0c/Garfield-comparison.png 1.5x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Garfield-comparison.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The appearance of the characters gradually changed over time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT1_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1-9">[9]</a></sup> The left panel is taken from the March 7, 1980, strip; the right is from the July 6, 1990, strip.</div></div></div>
<p>The strip underwent stylistic changes, evolving from the style of the 1976–83 strips, to a more cartoonish look from 1984 onward. This change has mainly affected Garfield's design, which underwent a "Darwinian evolution" in which he began walking on his hind legs, "slimmed down", and "stopped looking ... through squinty little eyes" His evolution, according to Davis, was to make it easier to "push Odie off the table" or "reach for a piece of pie".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT1_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Garfield</i> quickly became a commercial success. In 1981, less than three years after its nationwide launch, the strip appeared in 850 newspapers and accumulated over $15 million in merchandise. To manage the merchandise, Davis founded <a href="/wiki/Paws,_Inc." title="Paws, Inc.">Paws, Inc.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catty_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Catty-8">[8]</a></sup> In 1982 the strip was appearing in more than 1,000 newspapers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>By 2002, <i>Garfield</i> became the world's most syndicated strip, appearing in 2,570 newspapers with 263 million readers worldwide;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BW1_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-BW1-1">[1]</a></sup> by 2004, <i>Garfield</i> appeared in nearly 2,600 newspapers and sold from $750 million to $1 billion worth of merchandise in 111 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slatewhyhate_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-slatewhyhate-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1994, Davis's company, Paws, Inc., purchased all rights to the strips from 1978 to 1993 from United Feature.
</p><p>While retaining creative control and being the only signer, Davis now only writes and usually does the rough sketches. Since the late 1990s most of the work has been done by long-time assistants Brett Koth and Gary Barker. Inking and coloring work is done by other artists, while Davis spends most of the time supervising production and merchandising the characters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slatewhyhate_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-slatewhyhate-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Content">Content</span></h2>
<p>Part of the strip's broad pop cultural appeal is due to its lack of <a href="/wiki/Social_commentary" title="Social commentary">social</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_commentary#Political_cartoons" title="Political commentary">political</a> commentary; though this was Davis's original intention, he also admitted that his "grasp of politics isn't strong", joking that, for many years, he thought "<a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Dental_bonding" title="Dental bonding">denture adhesive</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>Originally created with the intentions to "come up with a good, marketable character",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wapocat_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-wapocat-14">[14]</a></sup> <i>Garfield</i> has spawned merchandise earning $750 million to $1 billion annually. In addition to the various merchandise and commercial tie-ins, the strip has spawned several animated television specials, two animated television series, two theatrical feature-length live-action/CGI animated films, and three fully CGI animated direct-to-video films.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Garfield_merchandise" title="Garfield merchandise">Garfield merchandise</a> and <a href="/wiki/Garfield_statues" title="Garfield statues">Garfield statues</a></div>
<p><i>Garfield</i> was originally created by Davis with the intention to come up with a "good, marketable character".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wapocat_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-wapocat-14">[14]</a></sup> Now the world's most syndicated comic strip,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> <i>Garfield</i> has spawned a "profusion"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slatewhyhate_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-slatewhyhate-11">[11]</a></sup> of merchandise including clothing, toys, games, books, Caribbean cruises, credit cards, dolls,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> DVDs of the movies or the TV series,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and related media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Books">Books</span></h3>
<p>Starting in 1980, the comic strip has been collected in anthologies. The first, <i>Garfield at Large</i>, was published in March 1980 by <a href="/wiki/Ballantine_Books" title="Ballantine Books">Ballantine Books</a>. These books helped increase the strip's popularity through sales, leading to several of them reaching the top of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i> best sellers list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pauer_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-pauer-19">[19]</a></sup> For these compilation books, Davis devised a book layout which is considerably longer and less tall than the average book. This allowed the strip to be oriented in the same format as it appeared in the newspaper, as opposed to earlier comic strip anthologies which often stacked the panels vertically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pauer_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-pauer-19">[19]</a></sup> This book style has since been referred to in the publishing industry as the "Garfield format" and has been adapted by other publishers. Davis noted that it became popular for other comic book anthologies in particular, such as those of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Far_Side" title="The Far Side">The Far Side</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet">Internet</span></h3>
<p>Garfield.com was the strip's official website, which contained archives of past strips along with games and an online store. Jim Davis had also collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Ball_State_University" title="Ball State University">Ball State University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pearson_Education" title="Pearson Education">Pearson</a> Digital Learning to create ProfessorGarfield.org, an educational website with interactive games focusing on math and reading skills, and with Children's Technology Group to create MindWalker, a web browser that allows parents to limit the websites their children can view to a preset list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>A variety of edited <i>Garfield</i> strips have been made available on the Internet, with some being hosted on their own unofficial, dedicated sites. Dating from 2005, a site called the "Garfield Randomizer" created a three-panel strip using panels from previous <i>Garfield</i> strips.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Another approach, known as "Silent Garfield",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> involved removing Garfield's thought balloons from the strips.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Some examples date from 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silentgarfield_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-silentgarfield-27">[27]</a></sup> A webcomic called <i>Arbuckle</i> does the above but also redraws the originals in a different art style. The <i>Arbuckle</i> website creator writes: "'Garfield' changes from being a comic about a sassy, corpulent feline, and becomes a compelling picture of a lonely, pathetic, delusional man who talks to his pets. Consider that Jon, according to Garfield canon, cannot hear his cat's thoughts. This is the world as he sees it. This is his story".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>Another variation along the same lines, called "Realfield" or "Realistic Garfield", was to redraw Garfield as a real cat and remove his thought balloons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tabby_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-tabby-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-realfield_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-realfield-30">[30]</a></sup> Still another approach to editing the strips involved removing Garfield and other main characters from the originals completely, leaving Jon talking to himself. While strips in this vein could be found online as early as 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silentgarfield_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-silentgarfield-27">[27]</a></sup> the 2008 site <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield_Minus_Garfield" title="Garfield Minus Garfield">Garfield Minus Garfield</a></i> by Dan Walsh received enough online attention to be covered by news media. Reception was largely positive: at its peak, the site received as many as 300,000 hits per day. Fans connected with Jon's "loneliness and desperation" and found his "crazy antics" humorous; Jim Davis himself called Walsh's strips an "inspired thing to do" and said that "some of [the strips] work better [than the originals]".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Ballantine Books, which publishes the <i>Garfield</i> books, released a volume of <i>Garfield Minus Garfield</i> strips on October 28, 2008. The volume retains Davis as author and features a foreword by Walsh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tabby_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-tabby-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 19, 2020, the website was shut down during the strip's 42nd anniversary, following Viacom's acquisition of Paws, Inc. in August 2019. The website now redirects to Nick.com, with an alternative link to GoComics.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television"><span class="anchor" id="Television"></span> Television</span></h3>
<p>Garfield's animation debut was on <i>The Fantastic Funnies</i>, which aired on CBS on May 15, 1980, voiced by actor <a href="/wiki/Scott_Beach" title="Scott Beach">Scott Beach</a>. <i>Garfield</i> was one of the strips featured, introduced as a newcomer (the strip was only two years old at the time). From 1982 to 1991, twelve primetime <i>Garfield</i> cartoon specials and one hour-long primetime documentary celebrating the character's 10th anniversary were aired; <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Music" title="Lorenzo Music">Lorenzo Music</a> voiced Garfield in all of them. A Saturday morning cartoon show, <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield_and_Friends" title="Garfield and Friends">Garfield and Friends</a></i>, aired for seven seasons from 1988 to 1994. This adaption also starred Music as the voice of Garfield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Garfield_Show" title="The Garfield Show">The Garfield Show</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">CGI</a> series, started development in 2007 to coincide with the strip's 30th anniversary in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> It premiered in France in December 2008 and made its U.S. debut on <a href="/wiki/Cartoon_Network" title="Cartoon Network">Cartoon Network</a> on November 2, 2009. A new series is currently in development at <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a> after <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Global" title="Paramount Global">Paramount Global</a> acquired the franchise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Films">Films</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Garfield:_The_Movie" title="Garfield: The Movie">Garfield: The Movie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garfield:_A_Tail_of_Two_Kitties" title="Garfield: A Tail of Two Kitties">Garfield: A Tail of Two Kitties</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Garfield_(2024_film)" title="Garfield (2024 film)">Garfield (2024 film)</a></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Live_action" title="Live action">live-action</a>/<a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">computed animated</a> film titled <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield:_The_Movie" title="Garfield: The Movie">Garfield: The Movie</a></i> was released in theaters on June 11, 2004 and a sequel titled <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield:_A_Tail_of_Two_Kitties" title="Garfield: A Tail of Two Kitties">Garfield: A Tail of Two Kitties</a></i> was released on June 16, 2006. Both films were released by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a> with actor <a href="/wiki/Bill_Murray" title="Bill Murray">Bill Murray</a> voicing the character in both films. Despite receiving negative reviews from critics, the films were both commercial successes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Three direct-to-video films were released by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox_Home_Entertainment" title="20th Century Fox Home Entertainment">20th Century Fox Home Entertainment</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield_Gets_Real" title="Garfield Gets Real">Garfield Gets Real</a></i> on November 20, 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield%27s_Fun_Fest" title="Garfield's Fun Fest">Garfield's Fun Fest</a></i> on August 5, 2008, and <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield%27s_Pet_Force" title="Garfield's Pet Force">Garfield's Pet Force</a></i> on June 16, 2009.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>On May 24, 2016, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Alcon_Entertainment" title="Alcon Entertainment">Alcon Entertainment</a> would develop a new CG animated <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield_(2024_film)" title="Garfield (2024 film)">Garfield</a></i> film, with John Cohen and Steven P. Wegner producing, and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Dindal" title="Mark Dindal">Mark Dindal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> In August 2019, <a href="/wiki/Viacom_(2005%E2%80%932019)" title="Viacom (2005–2019)">Viacom</a> acquired the rights to Garfield, leaving the status of the movie for the time uncertain, with Dindal confirming that the film was still in production in December 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steinberg_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Steinberg-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> On November 1, 2021, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Pratt" title="Chris Pratt">Chris Pratt</a> was announced as the voice of Garfield, with animation being provided by <a href="/wiki/DNEG" title="DNEG">DNEG</a>, a production company of the film. <a href="/wiki/David_Reynolds_(screenwriter)" title="David Reynolds (screenwriter)">David Reynolds</a> was announced as the screenwriter of the film, reuniting him with Dindal after they worked together on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Emperor%27s_New_Groove" title="The Emperor's New Groove">The Emperor's New Groove</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures" title="Sony Pictures">Sony Pictures</a> will maintain global distribution rights for the film, apart from China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>  On May 24, 2022, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_L._Jackson" title="Samuel L. Jackson">Samuel L. Jackson</a> joined the voice cast as Vic, Garfield’s father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> In September 2022, the film was scheduled to be released on May 24, 2024.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span></h3>
<p>A <i>Garfield</i> video game was developed by <a href="/wiki/Atari,_Inc." title="Atari, Inc.">Atari, Inc.</a> for its <a href="/wiki/Atari_2600" title="Atari 2600">Atari 2600</a> home <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_game_system" title="Video game system">video game system</a> and appears in their 1984 catalog.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> However, after <a href="/wiki/Atari_Corporation" title="Atari Corporation">Atari's spinoff and sale</a> of its home games and computers division, owner <a href="/wiki/Jack_Tramiel" title="Jack Tramiel">Jack Tramiel</a> decided the character's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royalties" title="Royalties">royalties</a> were too expensive given the <a href="/wiki/Video_game_crash_of_1983" title="Video game crash of 1983">declining state</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Video_game_industry" title="Video game industry">video game industry</a> at the time, and the game was cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-garfieldproto_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-garfieldproto-56">[56]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/ROM_image" title="ROM image">ROM image</a> of the game was however released with Jim Davis' blessing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-garfieldproto_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-garfieldproto-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Garfield:_Big_Fat_Hairy_Deal" title="Garfield: Big Fat Hairy Deal">Garfield: Big Fat Hairy Deal</a></i> is a 1987 video game for the <a href="/wiki/Atari_ST" title="Atari ST">Atari ST</a>, <a href="/wiki/ZX_Spectrum" title="ZX Spectrum">ZX Spectrum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commodore_64" title="Commodore 64">Commodore 64</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amstrad_CPC" title="Amstrad CPC">Amstrad CPC</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Amiga" title="Amiga">Amiga</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/Comic_strip" title="Comic strip">comic strip</a>. Towa Chiki made <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Week_of_Garfield" title="A Week of Garfield">A Week of Garfield</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Entertainment_System" title="Nintendo Entertainment System">Family Computer</a>, released only in Japan in 1989. <a href="/wiki/Sega" title="Sega">Sega</a> also made the 1995 video game <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield:_Caught_in_the_Act" title="Garfield: Caught in the Act">Garfield: Caught in the Act</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/Sega_Genesis" title="Sega Genesis">Sega Genesis/Mega Drive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Game_Gear" title="Game Gear">Game Gear</a> and Windows 3.1 computers. Other companies made games, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield:_A_Tail_of_Two_Kitties_(video_game)" title="Garfield: A Tail of Two Kitties (video game)">A Tale of Two Kitties</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">DS</a>, published by Game Factory, <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield%27s_Nightmare" title="Garfield's Nightmare">Garfield's Nightmare</a></i> for DS, <i>Garfield's Funfest</i> for DS, and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garfield_Labyrinth" title="Garfield Labyrinth">Garfield Labyrinth</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy" title="Game Boy">Game Boy</a>. On PlayStation 2 were <i>Garfield</i> and <i>Garfield 2</i> (known in the US as <i>Garfield, a Tale of Two Kitties</i>). <i>Garfield Lasagna World Tour</i> was also made for PS2. <i>Garfield: Saving Arlene</i> was only released in Japan and in the United Kingdom. And recent additions for mobile devices are "Garfield's Diner" and "Garfield's Zombie Defense".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Konami" title="Konami">Konami</a> also released a Garfield <a href="/wiki/Handheld_electronic_game" title="Handheld electronic game">handheld electronic game</a> titled <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lasagnator&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lasagnator (page does not exist)">Lasagnator</a></i> in 1991, which met with mild success.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In 2012, a series of Garfield video games was launched by French publisher <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anuman_Interactive" title="Anuman Interactive">Anuman Interactive</a>, including <i>My Puzzles with Garfield!</i>, <i>Multiplication Tables with Garfield</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield_Kart" title="Garfield Kart">Garfield Kart</a></i>, and <i>Garfield's Match Up</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p><p>Garfield appears as a playable character through free DLC for 2021's <i><a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_All-Star_Brawl" title="Nickelodeon All-Star Brawl">Nickelodeon All-Star Brawl</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stage">Stage</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Papp" title="Joseph Papp">Joseph Papp</a>, producer of <i><a href="/wiki/A_Chorus_Line" title="A Chorus Line">A Chorus Line</a></i>, discussed making a Garfield stage musical, but due to some complications, it never got off ground. A full-length stage musical, titled "Garfield Live", was planned to kick off its US tour in September 2010, but got moved to January 18, 2011, where it premiered in <a href="/wiki/Muncie,_Indiana" title="Muncie, Indiana">Muncie, Indiana</a>. The book was written by Jim Davis, with music and lyrics by Michael Dansicker and Bill Meade, and it was booked by AWA Touring Services. The opening song, "Cattitude" can be heard on the national tour's website, along with two more, "On the Fence", and "Going Home!".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> When the North-American tour concluded in 2012, it toured throughout Asia.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comic_book">Comic book</span></h3>
<p>In agreement with Paws, <a href="/wiki/Boom!_Studios" title="Boom! Studios">Boom! Studios</a> launched in May 2012 a monthly <i>Garfield</i> comic book, with the first issue featuring a story written by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Evanier" title="Mark Evanier">Mark Evanier</a> (who has supervised <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield_and_Friends" title="Garfield and Friends">Garfield and Friends</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Garfield_Show" title="The Garfield Show">The Garfield Show</a></i>) and illustrated by Davis's long-time assistant Gary Barker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_book">Art book</span></h3>
<p>In 2016, <a href="/wiki/Hermes_Press" title="Hermes Press">Hermes Press</a> signed an agreement with Paws, Inc to publish an art book on the art of author Jim Davis, titled <i>The Art of Jim Davis' Garfield</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herman_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herman-61">[61]</a></sup> The book includes an essay by author <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R.C._Harvey" title="R.C. Harvey">R.C. Harvey</a> and other original material, and was released in July 2016 for the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con" title="San Diego Comic-Con">San Diego Comic-Con</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herman_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-Herman-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Restaurant">Restaurant</span></h3>
<p>In 2018, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghost_restaurant" title="Ghost restaurant">ghost restaurant</a> themed after the franchise known as <a href="/wiki/GarfieldEats" title="GarfieldEats">GarfieldEATS</a> was opened in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>. Customers order food through the official mobile app, which also contains games and allows users to purchase episodes of <i>Garfield and Friends</i>. The restaurant serves lasagna, Garfield-shaped pizza, "<a href="/wiki/Cappuccino" title="Cappuccino">Garfuccinos</a>", and Garfield-shaped dark chocolate bars. A second location opened in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> as well as a dispute over rent, the restaurant closed in 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>
</p>

<p>Through the Garfield strips, there have been many additional characters, but the main ones are described here.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Garfield">Garfield</span></h3>
<p><b>First appearance: June 19, 1978</b>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><video class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="262" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Mike_Pence_Garfield_Speech.ogg" height="165" id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Mike_Pence_Garfield_Speech.ogg/220px--Mike_Pence_Garfield_Speech.ogg.jpg" preload="none" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="227792" data-framerate="29.97002997003" data-height="360" data-shorttitle="VP9 360P" data-title="VP9 (360P)" data-transcodekey="360p.vp9.webm" data-width="480" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/a/a0/Mike_Pence_Garfield_Speech.ogg/Mike_Pence_Garfield_Speech.ogg.360p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp8, vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="153456" data-framerate="29.97002997003" data-height="180" data-shorttitle="VP9 180P" data-title="Low bandwidth VP9 (180P)" data-transcodekey="180p.vp9.webm" data-width="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/a/a0/Mike_Pence_Garfield_Speech.ogg/Mike_Pence_Garfield_Speech.ogg.180p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1062260506">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:310px; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>I'm not overweight, I'm undertall.
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">—<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garfield_At_Large:_His_First_Book" title="Garfield At Large: His First Book">Garfield At Large: his First Book</a></i> (1980)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Garfield_(character)" title="Garfield (character)">Garfield</a> is an orange, fuzzy <a href="/wiki/Tabby_cat" title="Tabby cat">tabby cat</a> born in the kitchen of an Italian restaurant (later revealed in the television special <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield:_His_9_Lives#The_television_special" title="Garfield: His 9 Lives">Garfield: His 9 Lives</a></i> to be Mama Leoni's Italian Restaurant) who immediately ate all the pasta and lasagna in sight, thus developing his love and obsession for lasagna and <a href="/wiki/Pizza" title="Pizza">pizza</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup>
</p><p>Gags in the strips commonly deal with Garfield's obesity (in one strip, Jon jokes: "I wouldn't say Garfield is fat, but the last time he got on a <a href="/wiki/Ferris_wheel" title="Ferris wheel">Ferris wheel</a>, the two guys on top starved to death")<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> and his disdain of any form of exertion or work. He is known for saying "breathing is exercise".
</p><p>Though Garfield can be very cynical, he does have a soft side for his teddy bear, Pooky, food, and sleep, and during one Christmas he says, "They say I have to get up early, be nice to people, skip breakfast… I wish it would never end." However, in the feature film <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield_Gets_Real" title="Garfield Gets Real">Garfield Gets Real</a></i> and its sequels, Garfield is better behaved, friendlier towards Jon and Odie, less self-centered, and more sympathetic.
</p><p>It has been wondered by many readers if Garfield can actually be understood by the human characters around him. Sometimes, it seems like Jon can hear him. However, it is mentioned in more than one strip that Jon cannot understand Garfield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> However, in the feature film <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield_Gets_Real" title="Garfield Gets Real">Garfield Gets Real</a></i> and its sequels, Garfield and the other animals (save for Odie) are able to talk to, and be understood by, Jon and the other humans. In the April 1 (<a href="/wiki/April_Fools%27_Day" title="April Fools' Day">April Fools' Day</a>), 1997, strip drawn by the artists of <i><a href="/wiki/Blondie_(comic_strip)" title="Blondie (comic strip)">Blondie</a></i> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Comic_strip_switcheroo" title="Comic strip switcheroo">comic strip switcheroo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> Garfield, still with thought balloons, can be understood by Jon.
</p><p>To break the fourth wall, June 19 is celebrated within the strip as Garfield's birthday. The appearance in 1979 claimed it to be his first birthday, although in the first appearance of the strip (June 19, 1978), he was portrayed as a fully grown cat, implying that the birthday is for the strip itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jon_Arbuckle">Jon Arbuckle</span></h3>
<p><b>First appearance: June 19, 1978</b>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1062260506" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:310px; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p><i>Jon:</i> Here's my sixth-grade report card. My parents were so proud.<br/>
<i>Garfield, reading the report card:</i> "Jon has not shoved any crayons up his nose this term."
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">—<i>Garfield</i> (1996)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jon_Arbuckle" title="Jon Arbuckle">Jon</a> (Full name: Jonathan Q. Arbuckle) is Garfield's owner, usually depicted as an awkward clumsy <a href="/wiki/Geek" title="Geek">geek</a> who has trouble finding a date. Jon had a crush on Liz (Garfield's veterinarian) and is now dating her. Jon disapproves of Garfield's "don't care, not interested", attitude and often encourages his pet to take an interest in the world around him, sometimes stating an interesting fact or asking a philosophical question in an attempt to prompt Garfield into thought. Garfield tends to brush off these attempts with a simple yet logical remark, and despite the trouble Garfield causes, Jon has a heart of gold and is very tolerant of Garfield's shortcomings, a fact which Garfield often takes advantage of. In the December 23, 1980, strip, Jon states that he is thirty years old (nominally meaning he should presently be in his sixties, although he has not aged physically). His birthday is July 28.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jon loves (or occasionally hates) Garfield and all cats. Many gags focus on this; his inability to get a date is usually attributed to his lack of social skills, his poor taste in clothes (Garfield remarked in one strip after seeing his closet that "two hundred moths committed suicide";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> in another, the "geek police" ordered Jon to "throw out his tie"),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> and his eccentric interests which range from stamp collecting to measuring the growth of his toenails to watching movies with "<a href="/wiki/Polka" title="Polka">polka</a> <a href="/wiki/Ninja" title="Ninja">ninjas</a>". Other strips portray him as lacking intelligence (he is seen reading a <a href="/wiki/Pop-up_book" title="Pop-up book">pop-up book</a> in one strip).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jon was born on a farm that apparently contained few amenities; in one strip, his father, upon seeing indoor plumbing, remarks: "Woo-ha! Ain't science something?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> Jon occasionally visits his parents, brother and grandmother at their farm. It was implied that Jon is inspired by a drawing of Davis himself when he was first drawing the strip. Jon was portrayed as a <a href="/wiki/Cartoonist" title="Cartoonist">cartoonist</a> in the first strip<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> and occasional others in the early years; Davis stated his intent had been to express his own frustrations as a cartoonist. Ultimately, Jon's job has been referenced far more frequently in <i>Garfield</i> animated series than in the strip.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Odie">Odie</span></h3>
<p><b>First appearance: August 8, 1978</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1062260506" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:310px; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p><i>Jon:</i> I think I'm having some kind of identity crisis.
</p><p><i>Garfield, walking past Odie who is lying in a kitchen drawer:</i> He thinks <b>he's</b> having an identity crisis ... Odie thinks he's a potato peeler.
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">—<i>Garfield</i> (1991)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Odie" title="Odie">Odie</a> is a yellow, long-eared <a href="/wiki/Beagle" title="Beagle">beagle</a> with a large, slobbering tongue, who walks on all four legs, though occasionally he will walk on two like Garfield. He was originally owned by Jon's friend <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_Garfield#Lyman" title="List of characters in Garfield">Lyman</a>, though Jon adopted him after Lyman was written out of the strip. The book <i>Garfield: His 9 Lives</i> (1984) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Retcons" title="Retcons">retcons</a> Odie's origin: there is no mention of Lyman, and Odie was a puppy when he was acquired by Jon as company for Garfield (when Garfield was a kitten).
</p><p>Odie is younger than Garfield and usually portrayed as naïve, happy, affectionate and blissfully unaware of Garfield's cynical, sadistic nature, despite the physical abuse Garfield exhibits toward him, including regularly kicking him off the kitchen table or tricking him into going over the edge himself. On some occasions, however, he is depicted more intelligently, as in one strip, in which he holds a heavy rock to prevent Garfield from doing this, and actually hurts Garfield's foot. In one strip when Garfield and Jon are out of the house, Odie is seen reading <i><a href="/wiki/War_and_Peace" title="War and Peace">War and Peace</a></i> and watching <i>An Evening With Mozart</i> on television,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> but in "Ask a Dog" strips, he is depicted as illiterate and has to be read to by Garfield. Odie has only thought once. In another strip, published on January 28, 2010, he is seen solving Jon's <a href="/wiki/Sudoku" title="Sudoku">sudoku</a> puzzle.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dr._Liz_Wilson">Dr. Liz Wilson</span></h3>
<p><b>First appearance: June 26, 1979</b>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1062260506" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:310px; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p><i>Jon:</i> Tell me, Liz, haven't we met somewhere before? A rice paddy in Hong Kong?
</p><p><i>Liz:</i> Look, jerk. I'll be the vet for your cat, but I won't play <a href="/wiki/Fall_guy" title="Fall guy">fall guy</a> for your stupid lines. Understood?
</p><p><i>Jon, shocked:</i> Uh-huh. So long, doctor.
</p><p><i>Liz:</i> Have a nice day.
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">—<i>Garfield</i> (1979)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>Dr. Liz Wilson is Garfield and Odie's sarcastic <a href="/wiki/Veterinarian" title="Veterinarian">veterinarian</a> and a long time crush of Jon Arbuckle. She has a somewhat deadpan, sardonic persona and almost always reacts negatively to Jon's outlandish and goofball behavior but can even find it endearing on occasion. Jon often attempts to ask her out on a date, but rarely succeeds; however, in an extended story arc from June 20 to July 29, 2006 (with the main event taking place on July 28), Liz and Jon kiss, and have been a couple ever since.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recurring_subjects_and_themes">Recurring subjects and themes</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em 0.5em;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image{border:none;padding:2px 0 2px 0.5em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-imageright{border:none;padding:2px 0.5em 2px 0;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-empty-cell{border:none;padding:0;width:1px}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image-div{width:52px}html.client-js body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Garfield&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a> in this section. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2022</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Many of the gags focus on Garfield's obsessive eating and obesity; his dislike of spiders; his hatred of Mondays, diets, and any form of exertion; his constant shedding (which annoys Jon); and his abuse of Odie and Jon as well as his obsession with mailing Nermal to <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>, or simply throwing him <i>through</i> the front door. Though he will eat nearly anything (with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Raisin" title="Raisin">raisins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spinach" title="Spinach">spinach</a>), Garfield is particularly fond of <a href="/wiki/Lasagna" title="Lasagna">lasagna</a>; he also enjoys eating Jon's houseplants and other pets (mainly birds and fish).
</p><p>He also has odd relationships with household pests; Garfield generally spares mice, and even cooperates with them to cause mischief (much to Jon's chagrin), but will readily swat or pound spiders flat. Other gags focus on Jon's poor social skills and inability to get a date; before he started dating Liz, he often tried to get dates, usually without success (in one strip, after failing to get a date with "Nancy", he tries getting a date with her mother and grandmother; he ended up getting "shot down by three generations").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> When he does get a date, it usually goes awry; Jon's dates have slashed his tires, been tranquilized, and called the police when he stuck carrots in his ears. The storylines featuring Jon's dates rarely appear now. Before, he had dates with many odd characters, whereas now, he exclusively dates Liz.
</p><p>Garfield's world has specific locations that appear normally on the comic strips, like the vet's office (a place he loathes). Irma's Diner is another occasional setting. Irma is a chirpy but slow-witted and unattractive waitress/manager, and one of Jon's few friends. The terrible food is the center of most of the jokes, along with the poor management. Jon periodically visits his parents and brother on the farm. This results in week-long comical displays of stupidity by Jon and his family, and their interactions. There is a comic strip where Jon's brother Doc Boy is watching two socks in the dryer spinning and Doc Boy calls it entertainment.
</p><p>On the farm, Jon's mother will cook huge dinners; Garfield hugs her for this. Jon has a grandmother who, in a strip, once kicked Odie; Garfield subsequently hugged her. Jon's parents have twice visited Jon, Garfield, and Odie in the city. Jon's father drove into town on his <a href="/wiki/Tractor" title="Tractor">tractor</a> (which he <a href="/wiki/Double_parking" title="Double parking">double-parked</a>) and brought a rooster to wake him up. As Garfield has a love for food, they will often eat out at restaurants. Most trips end up embarrassing because Garfield will pig out, or Jon will do something stupid, including wearing an ugly shirt, which happened one night when he took Liz on a date. When Jon takes Liz on a date, Garfield occasionally tags along—once, he ate the bread and other food at an Italian restaurant they went to.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Garfield_Vault_Strip_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Garfield_Vault_Strip-87">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>Frequently, the characters break the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_wall" title="Fourth wall">fourth wall</a>, mostly to explain something to the readers, talk about a subject that often sets up the strip's punchline (like Jon claiming that pets are good for exercise right before he finds Garfield in the kitchen and chases him out),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> or give a mere glare when a character is belittled or not impressed. Sometimes, this theme revolves around the conventions of the strip; for example, in one strip, Garfield catches a cold and complains about it, noting that his thoughts are stuffed up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Short_storylines">Short storylines</span></h3>
<p>One particular semi-recurring storyline features Jon and Liz on a date in a restaurant. They sometimes are waited on by the Italian Armando, who is refined and sophisticated and shows a great loathing towards Jon, presumably for his immature and uncouth behavior at the prestigious eatery. On other occasions, the couple receives a different waiter, such as a large ogre-like man who intimidates Jon when he is about to report a complaint about the food.
</p><p>Another commonly recurring character, although hardly ever seen, is Jon's neighbor, Mrs. Feeny. Garfield seems to take both enormous pride and excess zeal in doing whatever it takes to harass her, to the point that she even erects an electric fence (which does not stop him).
</p><p>Other unique themes are things like "Garfield's Believe it or Don't",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> "Garfield's Law",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> "Garfield's History of Dogs",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> and "Garfield's History of Cats",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> which show science, history, and the world from Garfield's point of view. Another particular theme is "National Fat Week", where Garfield spends the week making fun of skinny people. Also, there was a storyline involving Garfield catching Odie eating his food and "kicking Odie into next week".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> Soon, Garfield realizes that "Lunch isn't the same without Odie. He always slips up behind me, barks loudly and makes me fall into my food" (Garfield subsequently falls into his food by himself).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p>A few days after the storyline began, Garfield is lying in his bed with a "nagging feeling I'm forgetting something", with Odie landing on Garfield in the next panel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> Jon and Liz began to go out more frequently. Jon has started hiring pet sitters to look after Garfield and Odie, though they do not always work out. Two particular examples are Lillian, an eccentric (and very nearsighted) old lady with odd quirks, and Greta, a muscle-bound woman who was hired to look after the pets during New Year's Eve.
</p><p>Most of December is spent preparing for Christmas, with a predictable focus on presents. Other Christmas themed strips include Jon's attempts at decorating the tree and house, or the attempt to buy the tree. Some years, the Christmas strips started as early as the end of November. Another example is "Splut Week", when Garfield tries to avoid pies that are thrown at him. For most of Garfield's history, being hit with a pie has inevitably resulted in the onomatopoeia "splut", hence the name.
</p><p>Every week before June 19, the strip focuses on Garfield's birthday, which he dreads because of his fear of getting older. This started happening after his sixth birthday. However, before his 29th birthday, Liz put Garfield on a diet. On June 19, 2007, Garfield was given the greatest birthday present: "I'M OFF MY DIET!" Occasionally the strip celebrates Halloween as well with scary-themed jokes, such as mask gags. There are also seasonal jokes, with snow-related gags common in January or February and beach- or heat-themed jokes in the summer.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:199px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Garfield_1989-10-27_right_panel.png"><img class="thumbimage" data-file-height="169" data-file-width="197" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/5a/Garfield_1989-10-27_right_panel.png" width="197"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption">Right panel of the October 27, 1989, strip</div></div></div>
<p>One storyline, which ran the week before <a href="/wiki/Halloween" title="Halloween">Halloween</a> in 1989, is unique among Garfield strips in that it is not meant to be humorous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (June 2019)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> It depicts Garfield awakening in a future in which the house is abandoned and he no longer exists. In Garfield's <i>Twentieth Anniversary Collection</i>, in which the strips are reprinted, Jim Davis discusses the genesis for this series:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>During a writing session for Halloween, I got the idea for this decidedly different series of strips. I wanted to scare people. And what do people fear most? Why, being alone. We carried out the concept to its logical conclusion and got a lot of responses from readers. Reaction ranged from 'Right on!' to 'This isn't a trend, is it?'</p></blockquote>
<p>One of the recurring storylines involves Garfield getting lost or running away. The longest one of these lasted for over a month (in 1986, from August 25 to September 28); it began with Jon telling Garfield to go get the newspaper. Garfield walks outside to get it, but speculates about what will happen if he wanders off – and decides to find out. Jon notices Garfield has been gone too long, so he sends Odie out to find him. He quickly realizes his mistake (Odie, being not too bright, also gets lost).
</p><p>Jon starts to get lonely, so he offers a reward for the return of Garfield and Odie. He is not descriptive, so animals including an elephant, <a href="/wiki/Monkey" title="Monkey">monkeys</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">seal</a>, a snake, a <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo" title="Kangaroo">kangaroo</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joey_(marsupial)" title="Joey (marsupial)">joey</a>, and turtles are brought to Jon's house for the reward. After a series of events, including Odie being adopted by a small girl, both pets meeting up at a circus that they briefly join, and both going to a pet shop, Garfield and Odie make it back home.
</p><p>Another story involved Jon going away on a business trip around Christmas time, leaving Garfield a week's worth of food, which he devoured instantly. Garfield then leaves the house and gets locked out. He then reunites with his mother, and eventually makes it back home in the snow on Christmas Eve (December 3–23, 1984). Part of this storyline was taken from the 1983 Emmy-winning special <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield_on_the_Town" title="Garfield on the Town">Garfield on the Town</a></i>.
</p>
<h2><span id="Paws.2C_Inc."></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Paws,_Inc.">Paws, Inc.</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Paws,_Inc." title="Paws, Inc.">Paws, Inc.</a></div>
<p>Paws, Inc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> was founded in 1981 by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Davis_(cartoonist)" title="Jim Davis (cartoonist)">Jim Davis</a> to support the Garfield comic strip and its licensing. It is located in <a href="/wiki/Muncie,_Indiana" title="Muncie, Indiana">Muncie, Indiana</a>, and has a staff of nearly 50 artists and licensing administrators. In 1994, the company purchased all rights to the Garfield comic strips from 1978 to 1993 from <a href="/wiki/United_Feature_Syndicate" title="United Feature Syndicate">United Feature Syndicate</a>. However, the original black and white daily strips and original color Sunday strips remain copyrighted to United Feature Syndicate. The full-color daily strips and recolored Sunday strips are copyrighted to Paws as they are considered a different product. Though rights to the strip remain with Paws, Inc., it is currently distributed by <a href="/wiki/Universal_Press_Syndicate" title="Universal Press Syndicate">Universal Press Syndicate</a>. In August 2019, Davis sold Paws, Inc. to <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Global" title="Paramount Global">Viacom</a>, who has placed Garfield under the <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a> banner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steinberg_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Steinberg-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p>

Vetvix is heavily based on Liz Wilson, right down to her design as well as her name being a reference to Liz's occupation as veterinarian.</span>
